# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Extension Registry and Factory Architecture

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the extension registry pattern: the Registry template class, the RegisterFactory macro usage, the factory lookup by name, and how extensions self-register at static initialization time.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of the Envoy extension registry pattern and saved it to `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary

The file contains a detailed examination of the extension registry pattern in envoyproxy/envoy v1.31.2, including:

### **Files (44+ C++ source files)**
- Core registry implementation: `envoy/registry/registry.h`
- Base factory classes: `envoy/config/typed_config.h`
- Configuration infrastructure: `source/server/`, `source/common/config/`
- 30+ extension implementations across HTTP filters, listener filters, access loggers, tracers, load balancers, and more

### **Key Symbols**
- `FactoryRegistry<Base>` - Template managing factory instances by name and type
- `RegisterFactory<T, Base>` - Template enabling static registration
- `FactoryCategoryRegistry` - Manages factory categories for discovery
- `UntypedFactory` / `TypedFactory` - Base classes for all factories
- Test utilities: `InjectFactory`, `InjectFactoryCategory`

### **How It Works**
The pattern leverages C++ static initialization to automatically register extension factories at program startup:

1. Extensions use the `REGISTER_FACTORY` macro to create a static `RegisterFactory` instance
2. The constructor registers the factory with `FactoryRegistry<BaseFactory>::registerFactory()`
3. Factories are looked up at runtime via `getFactory(name)` or `getFactoryByType(type_url)`
4. Each factory registers its category with `FactoryCategoryRegistry` for category-based discovery

The answer includes comprehensive code examples, line references, and explains the thread-safety model (safe for concurrent reads after initialization, single-threaded during registration).

Pattern Implementation\\n\\nThe Envoy proxy implements an extension registry pattern that enables dynamic, compile-time discovery and registration of extension factories. The architecture consists of several key components:\\n\\n### Core Components\\n\\n**1. Registry Template Class (envoy/registry/registry.h:166)**\\nThe `FactoryRegistry<Base>` template class is the central registry that manages all factory instances for a given base class. It maintains:\\n- A static factory map (hash map from name to factory pointer)\\n- Factories indexed by configuration type\\n- Versioning information for vendor-specific factories\\n- Deprecated factory name mappings\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `getFactory(name)` - Lookup factory by string name\\n- `getFactoryByType(type_url)` - Lookup by protobuf type\\n- `registerFactory(Base& factory, absl::string_view name)` - Runtime registration\\n- `registeredNames()` - List all registered factories\\n\\n**2. RegisterFactory Template Class (envoy/registry/registry.h:507)**\\nThe `RegisterFactory<T, Base>` template enables static registration of factory instances. When instantiated (typically at module load time), the constructor:\\n1. Creates a static instance of the concrete factory (T)\\n2. Registers it with `FactoryRegistry<Base>::registerFactory()`\\n3. Registers the factory's category with `FactoryCategoryRegistry`\\n\\nThe RegisterFactory constructor supports multiple overloads for:\\n- Basic registration\\n- Registration with deprecated names\\n- Registration with vendor-specific versions (major, minor, patch)\\n\\n**3. Macros (envoy/registry/registry.h:618-654)**\\nTwo macro variants handle static registration:\\n\\n`REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE)` - When `ENVOY_STATIC_EXTENSION_REGISTRATION` is defined:\\n```cpp\\nstatic Envoy::Registry::RegisterFactory<FACTORY, BASE> FACTORY##_registered;\\n```\\n\\nWhen not defined, it generates a function that dynamically creates the RegisterFactory:\\n```cpp\\nvoid forceRegister##FACTORY() {\\n  static auto registered = new Envoy::Registry::RegisterFactory<FACTORY, BASE>();\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**4. Factory Base Classes (envoy/config/typed_config.h)**\\n- `UntypedFactory` - Base with `name()` and `category()` methods\\n- `TypedFactory` - Extends UntypedFactory with `createEmptyConfigProto()` for protobuf configuration\\n\\n### Self-Registration at Static Initialization\\n\\nThe pattern leverages C++ static initialization to register factories:\\n\\n1. **Compile-time registration** (typical): Extensions define a static instance of `RegisterFactory<ConcreteFactory, BaseFactory>` at file scope, which runs during program initialization.\\n\\n2. **Example from source/extensions/filters/http/geoip/config.cc:35-36**:\\n```cpp\\nREGISTER_FACTORY(GeoipFilterFactory,\\n                 Server::Configuration::NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory){\\\"envoy.geoip\\\"};\\n```\\nThis expands to a static `RegisterFactory` instance that registers `GeoipFilterFactory` under the name \\\"envoy.geoip\\\".\\n\\n3. **Factory Category Registry**: Each factory also registers its category string (`UntypedFactory::category()` method) with `FactoryCategoryRegistry`, enabling discovery by category.\\n\\n### Factory Lookup Pattern\\n\\nAt runtime, extensions are discovered via two mechanisms:\\n\\n1. **By name lookup** (envoy/registry/registry.h:293):\\n```cpp\\nBase* getFactory(absl::string_view name) {\\n  auto it = factories().find(name);\\n  return (it == factories().end()) ? nullptr : it->second;\\n}\\n```\\n\\n2. **By protobuf type** (envoy/registry/registry.h:302):\\nThe `factoriesByType()` map is lazily built from all registered factories' `configTypes()`, enabling type-based lookup.\\n\\n### Configuration Implementation Files\\n\\n**Context and Utility Files:**\\n- `source/server/factory_context_impl.h` - FactoryContextImplBase for factory creation contexts\\n- `source/server/configuration_impl.h` - StatsSinkFactory and configuration management\\n- `source/common/config/utility.h` - Utility functions like `getAndCheckFactoryByName()` and `translateToFactoryConfig()`\\n\\n**Test Utilities (test/test_common/registry.h):**\\n- `InjectFactory<Base>` - Temporarily replaces a factory for testing\\n- `InjectFactoryCategory<Base>` - Registers a test category\\n\\n### Extension Implementation Pattern\\n\\nEach extension (found throughout source/extensions/) implements this pattern:\\n\\n1. **Header file** (e.g., config.h): Defines a factory class inheriting from `Config::TypedFactory` or base class specific to that extension type\\n2. **Implementation file** (e.g., config.cc): \\n   - Implements `createFilterFactoryFromProtoTyped()` or equivalent\\n   - Uses `REGISTER_FACTORY` macro at file scope for static registration\\n   - Looks up other factories via `Registry::FactoryRegistry<T>::getFactory()`\\n\\nExamples of this pattern appear in:\\n- HTTP filters (geoip, grpc_web, wasm, connect_grpc_bridge)\\n- Listener filters (tls_inspector, http_inspector, original_dst, proxy_protocol)\\n- Access loggers (fluentd, open_telemetry, stream)\\n- Tracers (opentelemetry, skywalking)\\n- Load balancing policies (maglev, cluster_provided)\\n- Stat sinks (dog_statsd, hystrix)\\n- And many more (48+ files in source/extensions/)\\n\\n### Thread Safety\\n\\nThe registry is **not thread-safe** during registration. Registration must occur in a single-threaded environment, guaranteed by static initialization happening before main() executes. All factory lookups after initialization are safe for concurrent access since the maps are only read, not modified.\\n\"\n}\n",

Pattern Implementation\\n\\nThe Envoy proxy implements an extension registry pattern that enables dynamic, compile-time discovery and registration of extension factories. The architecture consists of several key components:\\n\\n### Core Components\\n\\n**1. Registry Template Class (envoy/registry/registry.h:166)**\\nThe `FactoryRegistry<Base>` template class is the central registry that manages all factory instances for a given base class. It maintains:\\n- A static factory map (hash map from name to factory pointer)\\n- Factories indexed by configuration type\\n- Versioning information for vendor-specific factories\\n- Deprecated factory name mappings\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `getFactory(name)` - Lookup factory by string name\\n- `getFactoryByType(type_url)` - Lookup by protobuf type\\n- `registerFactory(Base& factory, absl::string_view name)` - Runtime registration\\n- `registeredNames()` - List all registered factories\\n\\n**2. RegisterFactory Template Class (envoy/registry/registry.h:507)**\\nThe `RegisterFactory<T, Base>` template enables static registration of factory instances. When instantiated (typically at module load time), the constructor:\\n1. Creates a static instance of the concrete factory (T)\\n2. Registers it with `FactoryRegistry<Base>::registerFactory()`\\n3. Registers the factory's category with `FactoryCategoryRegistry`\\n\\nThe RegisterFactory constructor supports multiple overloads for:\\n- Basic registration\\n- Registration with deprecated names\\n- Registration with vendor-specific versions (major, minor, patch)\\n\\n**3. Macros (envoy/registry/registry.h:618-654)**\\nTwo macro variants handle static registration:\\n\\n`REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE)` - When `ENVOY_STATIC_EXTENSION_REGISTRATION` is defined:\\n```cpp\\nstatic Envoy::Registry::RegisterFactory<FACTORY, BASE> FACTORY##_registered;\\n```\\n\\nWhen not defined, it generates a function that dynamically creates the RegisterFactory:\\n```cpp\\nvoid forceRegister##FACTORY() {\\n  static auto registered = new Envoy::Registry::RegisterFactory<FACTORY, BASE>();\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**4. Factory Base Classes (envoy/config/typed_config.h)**\\n- `UntypedFactory` - Base with `name()` and `category()` methods\\n- `TypedFactory` - Extends UntypedFactory with `createEmptyConfigProto()` for protobuf configuration\\n\\n### Self-Registration at Static Initialization\\n\\nThe pattern leverages C++ static initialization to register factories:\\n\\n1. **Compile-time registration** (typical): Extensions define a static instance of `RegisterFactory<ConcreteFactory, BaseFactory>` at file scope, which runs during program initialization.\\n\\n2. **Example from source/extensions/filters/http/geoip/config.cc:35-36**:\\n```cpp\\nREGISTER_FACTORY(GeoipFilterFactory,\\n                 Server::Configuration::NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory){\\\"envoy.geoip\\\"};\\n```\\nThis expands to a static `RegisterFactory` instance that registers `GeoipFilterFactory` under the name \\\"envoy.geoip\\\".\\n\\n3. **Factory Category Registry**: Each factory also registers its category string (`UntypedFactory::category()` method) with `FactoryCategoryRegistry`, enabling discovery by category.\\n\\n### Factory Lookup Pattern\\n\\nAt runtime, extensions are discovered via two mechanisms:\\n\\n1. **By name lookup** (envoy/registry/registry.h:293):\\n```cpp\\nBase* getFactory(absl::string_view name) {\\n  auto it = factories().find(name);\\n  return (it == factories().end()) ? nullptr : it->second;\\n}\\n```\\n\\n2. **By protobuf type** (envoy/registry/registry.h:302):\\nThe `factoriesByType()` map is lazily built from all registered factories' `configTypes()`, enabling type-based lookup.\\n\\n### Configuration Implementation Files\\n\\n**Context and Utility Files:**\\n- `source/server/factory_context_impl.h` - FactoryContextImplBase for factory creation contexts\\n- `source/server/configuration_impl.h` - StatsSinkFactory and configuration management\\n- `source/common/config/utility.h` - Utility functions like `getAndCheckFactoryByName()` and `translateToFactoryConfig()`\\n\\n**Test Utilities (test/test_common/registry.h):**\\n- `InjectFactory<Base>` - Temporarily replaces a factory for testing\\n- `InjectFactoryCategory<Base>` - Registers a test category\\n\\n### Extension Implementation Pattern\\n\\nEach extension (found throughout source/extensions/) implements this pattern:\\n\\n1. **Header file** (e.g., config.h): Defines a factory class inheriting from `Config::TypedFactory` or base class specific to that extension type\\n2. **Implementation file** (e.g., config.cc): \\n   - Implements `createFilterFactoryFromProtoTyped()` or equivalent\\n   - Uses `REGISTER_FACTORY` macro at file scope for static registration\\n   - Looks up other factories via `Registry::FactoryRegistry<T>::getFactory()`\\n\\nExamples of this pattern appear in:\\n- HTTP filters (geoip, grpc_web, wasm, connect_grpc_bridge)\\n- Listener filters (tls_inspector, http_inspector, original_dst, proxy_protocol)\\n- Access loggers (fluentd, open_telemetry, stream)\\n- Tracers (opentelemetry, skywalking)\\n- Load balancing policies (maglev, cluster_provided)\\n- Stat sinks (dog_statsd, hystrix)\\n- And many more (48+ files in source/extensions/)\\n\\n### Thread Safety\\n\\nThe registry is **not thread-safe** during registration. Registration must occur in a single-threaded environment, guaranteed by static initialization happening before main() executes. All factory lookups after initialization are safe for concurrent access since the maps are only read, not modified.\\n\"\n}\n",

Registers the factory's category with `FactoryCategoryRegistry`\\n\\nThe RegisterFactory constructor supports multiple overloads for:\\n- Basic registration\\n- Registration with deprecated names\\n- Registration with vendor-specific versions (major, minor, patch)\\n\\n**3. Macros (envoy/registry/registry.h:618-654)**\\nTwo macro variants handle static registration:\\n\\n`REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE)` - When `ENVOY_STATIC_EXTENSION_REGISTRATION` is defined:\\n```cpp\\nstatic Envoy::Registry::RegisterFactory<FACTORY, BASE> FACTORY##_registered;\\n```\\n\\nWhen not defined, it generates a function that dynamically creates the RegisterFactory:\\n```cpp\\nvoid forceRegister##FACTORY() {\\n  static auto registered = new Envoy::Registry::RegisterFactory<FACTORY, BASE>();\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**4. Factory Base Classes (envoy/config/typed_config.h)**\\n- `UntypedFactory` - Base with `name()` and `category()` methods\\n- `TypedFactory` - Extends UntypedFactory with `createEmptyConfigProto()` for protobuf configuration\\n\\n### Self-Registration at Static Initialization\\n\\nThe pattern leverages C++ static initialization to register factories:\\n\\n1. **Compile-time registration** (typical): Extensions define a static instance of `RegisterFactory<ConcreteFactory, BaseFactory>` at file scope, which runs during program initialization.\\n\\n2. **Example from source/extensions/filters/http/geoip/config.cc:35-36**:\\n```cpp\\nREGISTER_FACTORY(GeoipFilterFactory,\\n                 Server::Configuration::NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory){\\\"envoy.geoip\\\"};\\n```\\nThis expands to a static `RegisterFactory` instance that registers `GeoipFilterFactory` under the name \\\"envoy.geoip\\\".\\n\\n3. **Factory Category Registry**: Each factory also registers its category string (`UntypedFactory::category()` method) with `FactoryCategoryRegistry`, enabling discovery by category.\\n\\n### Factory Lookup Pattern\\n\\nAt runtime, extensions are discovered via two mechanisms:\\n\\n1. **By name lookup** (envoy/registry/registry.h:293):\\n```cpp\\nBase* getFactory(absl::string_view name) {\\n  auto it = factories().find(name);\\n  return (it == factories().end()) ? nullptr : it->second;\\n}\\n```\\n\\n2. **By protobuf type** (envoy/registry/registry.h:302):\\nThe `factoriesByType()` map is lazily built from all registered factories' `configTypes()`, enabling type-based lookup.\\n\\n### Configuration Implementation Files\\n\\n**Context and Utility Files:**\\n- `source/server/factory_context_impl.h` - FactoryContextImplBase for factory creation contexts\\n- `source/server/configuration_impl.h` - StatsSinkFactory and configuration management\\n- `source/common/config/utility.h` - Utility functions like `getAndCheckFactoryByName()` and `translateToFactoryConfig()`\\n\\n**Test Utilities (test/test_common/registry.h):**\\n- `InjectFactory<Base>` - Temporarily replaces a factory for testing\\n- `InjectFactoryCategory<Base>` - Registers a test category\\n\\n### Extension Implementation Pattern\\n\\nEach extension (found throughout source/extensions/) implements this pattern:\\n\\n1. **Header file** (e.g., config.h): Defines a factory class inheriting from `Config::TypedFactory` or base class specific to that extension type\\n2. **Implementation file** (e.g., config.cc): \\n   - Implements `createFilterFactoryFromProtoTyped()` or equivalent\\n   - Uses `REGISTER_FACTORY` macro at file scope for static registration\\n   - Looks up other factories via `Registry::FactoryRegistry<T>::getFactory()`\\n\\nExamples of this pattern appear in:\\n- HTTP filters (geoip, grpc_web, wasm, connect_grpc_bridge)\\n- Listener filters (tls_inspector, http_inspector, original_dst, proxy_protocol)\\n- Access loggers (fluentd, open_telemetry, stream)\\n- Tracers (opentelemetry, skywalking)\\n- Load balancing policies (maglev, cluster_provided)\\n- Stat sinks (dog_statsd, hystrix)\\n- And many more (48+ files in source/extensions/)\\n\\n### Thread Safety\\n\\nThe registry is **not thread-safe** during registration. Registration must occur in a single-threaded environment, guaranteed by static initialization happening before main() executes. All factory lookups after initialization are safe for concurrent access since the maps are only read, not modified.\\n\"\n}\n",
